  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_94c14abe-c72d-4bfd-8384-bfab4f46b8f7'
      });

<div id="review_1050691884" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1050691884" />
    <a title="Courtney Wells" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19433724-courtney-wells"><img alt="Courtney Wells" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392617868p2/19433724.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1050691884?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Courtney Wells" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Courtney Wells" href="/user/show/19433724-courtney-wells">Courtney Wells</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=oh-the-inhumanity">oh-the-inhumanity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=unbridled-sarcasm-ensued">unbridled-sarcasm-ensued</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=murder-and-or-mayhem">murder-and-or-mayhem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19433724-courtney-wells?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050691884" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6312740532096233718">Just when I think I'm over vampire books they SUCK ME BACK IN!<br/><br/>Basically what happened was I this: I browsed some indie titles and - after reading the synopsis - just gave the woman my money. <br/><br/>I'm sorry - a girl inherits house with a basement full of "danger" sounded like such a simplistic/brilliant way to just get into the action without so much pomp and pretext! Seriously, sometimes the direct approach just works wonders on my wallet.<br/><br/>So HIDDEN is exactly what it says on the tin and - because of </span>
  <span id="freeText6312740532096233718" style="display:none">Just when I think I'm over vampire books they SUCK ME BACK IN!<br /><br />Basically what happened was I this: I browsed some indie titles and - after reading the synopsis - just gave the woman my money. <br /><br />I'm sorry - a girl inherits house with a basement full of "danger" sounded like such a simplistic/brilliant way to just get into the action without so much pomp and pretext! Seriously, sometimes the direct approach just works wonders on my wallet.<br /><br />So HIDDEN is exactly what it says on the tin and - because of that basic hook and plot - gets to really invest in a) character development, b) establishing beautiful scenes, c) provide snappy humor, in and out of dialogue. Reading this reminded me that sometimes books get bogged down with world-building and mythos. While it's usually amazing when an author gets to explore the method to whatever madness their story is set in it also can get exhausting to absorb. That was why it was sort of refreshing that HIDDEN wasn't trying to be something other than just itself and it's all the more charming for that.<br /><br />Madison is a protagonist for readers who appreciate a little brash and crass. She has "screw-up" practically stamped on her head but Shalini Boland gives her enough redeemable qualities and good intentions to make her relateable and vulnerable in various places. <br /><br />All that held back a 5-star review was the random, unannounced shifts in POV between narrators. I'm sure authors intend for this to be a streaming flow of consciousness or seamless shift to other pertinent information but for me it's like walking down the sidewalk, catching my toe on a crack and desperately grabbing my barrings. Those shifts kept jarring me out of the story, which always gets irksome for me whenever I read. <br /><br />Beyond that, HIDDEN is great for what it is - teen vampire romance. It is edgy without getting too trashy. It's romantic without being super sappy. It doesn't think it's funny or try to be - it just is. And - topping it all off - some of the descriptions and turns of phrase are so eloquent, vivid and/or clever it's a truly impressive show compared to the usual plain-talk and prose found in YA.<br /><br />I highly recommend HIDDEN if you have a soft-spot for books like TWILIGHT or THE VAMPIRE DIARIES but appreciate less swooning and sassier protagonists.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6312740532096233718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_583586127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/583586127" />

When I picked it up I didn't know much about it except that it was about vampires. I didn't realise it was going to be like a mixture of Dracula and Twilight. <br /><br />This is a new twist on the vampire lore, whilst at the same time maintaining the dark suspense from traditional vampire books. I think many of us have fantasised at least once about some distant relative we didn't know about leaving us a ton of money and a gorgeous old house, well this actually happens for sixteen year old Madison and she and her brother move into Marchwood, which puts Downton Abbey to shame, with her little brother. <div id="review_217396131" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217396131" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4593305-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290988959p2/4593305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217396131?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/4593305-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217396131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8572957787061697324">I’m torn. This was a book that had me hooked in parts and feeling less enthusiastic in others. Although I enjoyed much of it, there were elements that felt too familiar, like I’d “been there, read that”.<br/><br/>In the beginning, the author does a great job of telling the story as if it were two separate books, using alternating points of view and experiences. She intertwines the past and the present in a very satisfying way, giving each character their fair share of time and attention. Some might feel t</span>
  <span id="freeText8572957787061697324" style="display:none">I’m torn. This was a book that had me hooked in parts and feeling less enthusiastic in others. Although I enjoyed much of it, there were elements that felt too familiar, like I’d “been there, read that”.<br /><br />In the beginning, the author does a great job of telling the story as if it were two separate books, using alternating points of view and experiences. She intertwines the past and the present in a very satisfying way, giving each character their fair share of time and attention. Some might feel that it takes too long to set up the story, but it was the set up that I found most fascinating. It held my attention and made me want to keep reading.<br /><br />I felt myself very drawn to Alexandre’s story. His experiences in Paris and on the archaeological expedition in the 19th century were unique. It was a different world, a different time, and it stimulated my imagination. There was drama, mystery and humor, and Alexandre is an intelligent character who is well-rounded and written in a very endearing way. The cast of characters in his world felt very real and their relationships were interesting.<br /><br />In contrast, Madison’s story felt less believable. Living in modern-day London in foster care, she discovers that a long-lost relative has left her money and a huge home. Now, I can buy that…I’m sure it happens to people…somewhere! But it’s the fact that she moves to this new home alone with her young brother and chooses to quit school that confuses me. She’s 16. How is this allowed to happen? Yes, I know…it’s a book and I should suspend judgement but this part of the plot dampened my enjoyment of the book just a little. Don’t get me wrong, Madison is a spunky character who looks at life in a unique way and stands up for what she believes in. She looks after her brother with motherly care and has a great curiosity about the world. She’s self-sufficient and smart. But she’s still just 16 and I’m not sure her circumstances and decisions are convincing enough for me.<br /><br />Ultimately, this is a vampire story….well, a vampire love story. I like the fact that this vampire world is different from those I’ve read about lately. These vampires are more traditional in their heritage and characteristics…they’re more mythical and scarier. The love story, however, is not as unique. Usually the romance in a book brings out my girly side and I fall in love with the “falling in love”. However, in this book, this is exactly where I started to see familiar themes and felt a bit let down. Although the romance is well written, it’s just too predictable for me.<br /><br />I must say that I was surprised by the ending! It was very unexpected…bringing back the uniqueness of the first half of the book. It definitely makes me curious about where the author will take the story next.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8572957787061697324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184327606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184327606" />
    <a title="Rayven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4730325-rayven"><img alt="Rayven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293845181p2/4730325.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184327606?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rayven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rayven" href="/user/show/4730325-rayven">Rayven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184327606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15733127566699543206">Hidden is the first book in the Marchwood Vampire Series by Shalini Boland. This story is a breath of fresh air in the young adult paranormal genre. Spanning centuries and continents, this lively story takes us on an intriguing journey of discovery and horror that you don't want to end. The story follows Madison Greene and her brother Ben, as their lives take a dramatic turn for the better. Moving out of foster care into their own home and immense wealth. But along with the wealth comes responsi</span>
  <span id="freeText15733127566699543206" style="display:none">Hidden is the first book in the Marchwood Vampire Series by Shalini Boland. This story is a breath of fresh air in the young adult paranormal genre. Spanning centuries and continents, this lively story takes us on an intriguing journey of discovery and horror that you don't want to end. The story follows Madison Greene and her brother Ben, as their lives take a dramatic turn for the better. Moving out of foster care into their own home and immense wealth. But along with the wealth comes responsibility and intrigue. In this tale we see the past merge with the present in a chilling and exciting way, as Madison searches for answers and finds them from the most unexpected person ; Alexander Chevalier whom just happens to be a vampire.<br /><br /><br />The characters within the novel come to life and jump right off the page, I found myself easily immersed in the story from the late Victorian era of Alexandre's journey to Cappadocia, where he and his family unlock pure evil, then submerged into Madison's world of dealing with the present. The characters have depth and are very well rounded, along with the supporting characters that bring more insights and comical humor to the story. The love story is very well portrayed and done tastefully and well suited for a young adult audience. I found myself once again caught up in the feelings of first love. <br /><br /><br />This book is extremely well written and I was very impressed with the author's ability to tell two stories in completely different styles of writing; late Victorian for Alexandre's story, and present day for Madison's. She did a fantastic job and both stories flowed well throughout the entire book to merge into a great ending. One of the things I really enjoyed about this novel, was the author's ability to create terrifying and chilling scenes within the book. She led me through my own imagination as my mind brought up images of what was taking place. Much to my surprise I might add since I love gritty detail. The author also had a way with humor as the characters interacted in a truly comical way when Alexandre a Victorian Noble tries to find is way in the modern world.<br /><br /><br />All in all this book was a great read and I recommend it to anyone who loves a good vampire story. This is a unique tale that stands out among the rest due to the author's wonderful storytelling and her fresh new perspective on Vampires. I am looking forward to reading the next book in series "Thicker than Blood, Book 2" I give this book 4.5 Stars!<br /><br />Reviewed for DarkissReads. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.darkissreads.com">www.darkissreads.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15733127566699543206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247816890?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.S. Einfeld" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.S. Einfeld" href="/user/show/7070022-c-s-einfeld">C.S. Einfeld</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247816890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12088939035085454408">HIDDEN by Shalini Boland is a YA paranormal romance that delivers, and then some. Madison Greene is the Goth girl we all secretly (or not so secretly), want to be: tough, cool, smart. She's also dealing with some very serious issues: foster-care, borderline-abusive adults, and keeping her little bro, Ben, safe and as carefree as possible in a very dodgy environment. Now, throw in a cadre of ancient, breathtakingly beautiful vampires, and the stage is set for intrigue to ensue.<br/><br/>So far, we've cover</span>
  <span id="freeText12088939035085454408" style="display:none">HIDDEN by Shalini Boland is a YA paranormal romance that delivers, and then some. Madison Greene is the Goth girl we all secretly (or not so secretly), want to be: tough, cool, smart. She's also dealing with some very serious issues: foster-care, borderline-abusive adults, and keeping her little bro, Ben, safe and as carefree as possible in a very dodgy environment. Now, throw in a cadre of ancient, breathtakingly beautiful vampires, and the stage is set for intrigue to ensue.<br /><br />So far, we've covered some of the things you might expect in the genre but, here are some things that I think make Hidden a cut-above:<br /><br />- The history of the Vampires. It's hard to detail too much without including any spoilers but, let's just say, their story, all on its own, would be enough for me to recommend this book. Boland masterfully weaves snippets of RL Turkish history and the magnificent Cappadocian caves with a new twist on traditional Vampire lore. I'm impressed, and now I need to visit Turkey.<br /><br />- Alexandre. Yes, yes, he's beautiful, and powerful, and all things sexy as every good vampire hottie should be. But, he's also achingly vulnerable. He needs Maddy as much as she needs him and together, they complete each other. Again, Boland knocks the romance side of the story out of the park.<br /><br />- The Intrigue. There were parts of the story where I found myself really miffed with Ms. Boland. Not because she failed to engage me, but because I really needed to put HIDDEN down to go off to take care of other RL obligations, but couldn't! WHAT is behind that cellar door? WHAT is buried under the Turkish desert? WHO is screaming and WHAT are they screaming AT??? That's just a partial list, but you get the point. Is this book a bona-fide "page-turner"? Yes, indeed it is.<br /><br />So, with that, a hearty FIVE STAR recommendation from me. :o)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12088939035085454408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6350351379768036601">Updating this (sorry Shalini for the delay)<br/><br/>This was a really great YA Paranormal Romance. It starts out a bit slow because the author is catching you up to how/why it all started so there is some past mixed with the present but the author does a great job. The paranormal part doesn't start right away (maybe halfway through the book?) but you can tell it creeps up on the paranormal aspect from the storyline and what's going on.... you know there's something there but you don't know what. When it </span>
  <span id="freeText6350351379768036601" style="display:none">Updating this (sorry Shalini for the delay)<br /><br />This was a really great YA Paranormal Romance. It starts out a bit slow because the author is catching you up to how/why it all started so there is some past mixed with the present but the author does a great job. The paranormal part doesn't start right away (maybe halfway through the book?) but you can tell it creeps up on the paranormal aspect from the storyline and what's going on.... you know there's something there but you don't know what. When it finally happens you're like "Oh, that's where it was going." it makes perfect sense. Even without the paranormal elements in the first half of the book it still kept my attention with intrigue and surprises. I'm more of an adult paranormal romance girl but I can enjoy YA once in awhile and I really enjoyed this one by the author. <br /><br />If you enjoy a bit of mystery, romance, intrigue, Paranormal give this book a try. I like how the vampires come into play...its not like normal vampire books where one guy swoons/bites one girl and converts her...no, its a bit more dark and mysterious than that. Give Shalini a try :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6350351379768036601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_242512647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242512647" />
    <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin"><img alt="Shaz Goodwin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605022219p2/4422203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/242512647?book_show_action=true">Dec 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaz Goodwin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaz Goodwin" href="/user/show/4422203-shaz-goodwin">Shaz Goodwin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer242512647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13851579463568815005">I really enjoy reading a story that encompasses two different timelines. To me, this makes it much more interesting. We know there is a connection and the intrigue is in trying to work out how they connect. Hidden is no exception. I loved reading about Paris in 1881 and the two families journey to Turkey. Alongside that, I also loved reading about Maddie in the present day. Each timeline has its crisis point until the timelines merge.<br/><br/>The characters are brilliantly portrayed. The leads, Maddie an</span>
  <span id="freeText13851579463568815005" style="display:none">I really enjoy reading a story that encompasses two different timelines. To me, this makes it much more interesting. We know there is a connection and the intrigue is in trying to work out how they connect. Hidden is no exception. I loved reading about Paris in 1881 and the two families journey to Turkey. Alongside that, I also loved reading about Maddie in the present day. Each timeline has its crisis point until the timelines merge.<br /><br />The characters are brilliantly portrayed. The leads, Maddie and Alexandre just took up residence in my life and I couldn’t stop thinking about them, even when I wasn’t reading about them. Maddie is so down to earth and caring despite the trauma of her father leaving during her mum’s pregnancy with Ben … and then her mum’s death when she was eight after which she spent so many years in care homes and foster care. She still has a fear about the world she lives in but it doesn’t paralyse her – she is a very strong character. Alexandre is HOT. Scorching hot! Besides his physique, there is a lot to endear him to the reader. Boland lets the reader right into his psyche and it’s interesting to watch his arrogance in 1881 and then his vulnerability in the present day. The characters on the periphery are all solid. I didn’t like solicitor Vasey-Smith from the very first moment he entered the story and even though he did everything right for Maddie I sensed something underlying in his character. He was way too smooth…<br /><br />Alexandre and Maddie’s love is very refreshing. Maddie’s feelings begin with awe, change into anger and hatred and finally develop into something stomach churning and bone melting (in a good way!) Despite the depth of her feelings there is also an innocence about it all. Their relationship doesn’t get started till quite a way through the story and I’m so looking forward to seeing how this develops in the second book.<br /><br />The environment is very apt for a paranormal read. The estate in Tetbury is isolated with only the Morris’ as caretakers for Maddie and Ben. In Turkey, the exploration and then discovery of the underground city is full of tension. Quite a lot of activity takes place in ‘basements’ without light but with shadows. Even when the timelines merge, at crisis points outside of Marchwood, they are full of tension. It’s not all ‘dark’ though as this is balanced by the romance!<br /><br />Hidden is not your average vampire story. The vampires themselves are not your usual run-of-the-mill type. It’s hard to say why they are different as its all a part of the weave and weft in the tale but it does cause an anomaly, which is quite central to the final crisis. This crisis is very dramatic and nail biting which I loved! The tension, fear, relief, then tension, fear and hope repeated is a double whammy.<br /><br />Boland’s writing carried me along and allowed me to experience many emotions in this world she has created.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend Hidden if you like YA, paranormal romance or vampires. Even if this isn’t your usual genre, I think you may well be surprised. At only £1.99 on Kindle (Amazon) at the time of my review, my recommendation is to buy a copy for yourself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13851579463568815005" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_574445746" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/574445746" />
    <a title="Zili" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18851333-zili"><img alt="Zili" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520252593p2/18851333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/574445746?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zili" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zili" href="/user/show/18851333-zili">Zili</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18851333-zili?shelf=fantasy-ya">fantasy-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18851333-zili?shelf=vamps-ya">vamps-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer574445746" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17822893061314222230">As a big fan of anything vampire and history related this was right up my street. Like so many kids I was obsessed with Room 13 (where an evil vampire lives in a hidden room, in a creepy old hotel). <br/><br/>Hidden tells the duel stories of modern day British teenager Madison, and of Alexandre, a French teenager living in the 1800s. Shalini cleverly weaves both stories together until Maddy and Alex eventually meet. Alex and his family leave France to hunt for a lost Turkish village where they face a trag</span>
  <span id="freeText17822893061314222230" style="display:none">As a big fan of anything vampire and history related this was right up my street. Like so many kids I was obsessed with Room 13 (where an evil vampire lives in a hidden room, in a creepy old hotel). <br /><br />Hidden tells the duel stories of modern day British teenager Madison, and of Alexandre, a French teenager living in the 1800s. Shalini cleverly weaves both stories together until Maddy and Alex eventually meet. Alex and his family leave France to hunt for a lost Turkish village where they face a tragedy which spans the years and miles into modern England. Having spent years living in foster care, Maddy and her brother Ben inherit the huge Marchwood estate (and £61 million). Whilst Ben goes to school, the now rich Maddy investigates the house, finding a hidden door in the basement which holds many dark secrets. I really enjoyed Shalini's twist on the vampire legend (coming from Turkey not Transylvania) and her detailed descriptions of both nineteenth century and modern life. There were times when I wanted the narrative to get a move on so Maddy and Alex could meet. <br /><br />Maddy is sassy and forward, but at times she is immature and bratty. Shalini does however manage to make her likeable and interesting. Maddy is totally different from the reserved ladylike girls from Alex's time, but they find each other fascinating and so the story works. The romance is kept to kissing and cuddling, to the point where I felt that we had another Meyer on our hands. I may be cynical but I find it hard to believe that beautiful teenagers living together in modern times away from the constraints of courtly love, with no adult supervision or rules would stick to cuddling. I suppose that the point though is that in Alex's time he causes a scandal from just kissing a girl.<br /><br />My Aunt lived in a huge ancient house complete with hidden rooms, stairs, trapdoors and like in Hidden; a secret door in the basement. I've never forgotten that secret door and Hidden had me hooked from the off (I never did manage to open the door)! Hidden is the first in a trilogy, with the next instalment Thicker Than Blood already released.<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://ziliinthesky.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">See my blog for more reviews</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17822893061314222230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_155365015" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155365015" />
    <a title="B. Lloyd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5141792-b-lloyd"><img alt="B. Lloyd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442638547p2/5141792.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155365015?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B. Lloyd" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B. Lloyd" href="/user/show/5141792-b-lloyd">B. Lloyd</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155365015" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5105093439475589299">Vampires, an inheritance with a secret, archaeology, scary men in white coats : all classic ingredients in this upbeat retelling of the vampyr legend. <br/><br/>HIDDEN breaks with Transylvanian tradition by placing the vampires deep under the soil of Cappadocia where two archaeologists take their families excavating in 1881, triggering off a series of terrifying adventures. <br/>In this timespill narrative, the lives of 19th century Alexandre and 21st century Maddy cross over in a tantalizing weave, rushing he</span>
  <span id="freeText5105093439475589299" style="display:none">Vampires, an inheritance with a secret, archaeology, scary men in white coats : all classic ingredients in this upbeat retelling of the vampyr legend. <br /><br />HIDDEN breaks with Transylvanian tradition by placing the vampires deep under the soil of Cappadocia where two archaeologists take their families excavating in 1881, triggering off a series of terrifying adventures. <br />In this timespill narrative, the lives of 19th century Alexandre and 21st century Maddy cross over in a tantalizing weave, rushing headlong towards an uncertain future. <br /><br />Here is a book crammed with colour: Byzantine imagery, Victorian charm and a Thoroughly Modern Milly - that is, Maddy, an orphaned teenager in the 21st century who suddenly comes into an inheritance. She and her brother move into Marchwood House and begin exploring, only(as might be expected in a paranormal story) nothing is quite as it seems. An iron door in the cellar hides secrets over a hundred years old and through a series of chilling events, the story of the Cappadocian expedition is pieced together along with its impact on Maddy and Alexandre's lives. <br /><br />The image of the vampire has haunted many cultures, both East and West, yet curiously there is little reference to them in Turkish folklore - although there is an interesting connection :Vlad Tepes, later Dracula, grew up during a period of semi-fealty to Turkey when his father paid tribute to the Sultan. Bloodthirsty reprisals illustrate most of Vlad's life in his efforts to free his country and he passed into legend as a hero to his own people, until Bram Stoker came across his name in a Whitby library book and spawned a literary genre that is flourishing healthily today. <br /><br />HIDDEN is a new-comer to this tradition and is the first of a trilogy : it is a fast paced, lively narrative, a fun, imaginative YA read (and quite likely to appeal to other audiences), with some unusual twists and turns. Very visual writing (I can imagine this being televised), with the potential to develop quite a following.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5105093439475589299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175560787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16388965388139329544">WHAT I THOUGHT<br/><br/>Phew, I’m glad I didn’t miss out on this one is what I thought.<br/><br/>I have not read many vampire books and admit they don’t hold a lot of appeal for me. However, I am so happy I accepted to review Shalini Boland’s excellent book <i>Hidden</i> and am grateful for this reading experience I may not have otherwise had. <br/><br/>What can I say? It wasn’t what I expected. I loved it. I was completely sucked in and didn’t want to put it down. One might say I was captivated. <br/><br/>Now, I have to be careful here not </span>
  <span id="freeText16388965388139329544" style="display:none">WHAT I THOUGHT<br /><br />Phew, I’m glad I didn’t miss out on this one is what I thought.<br /><br />I have not read many vampire books and admit they don’t hold a lot of appeal for me. However, I am so happy I accepted to review Shalini Boland’s excellent book <i>Hidden</i> and am grateful for this reading experience I may not have otherwise had. <br /><br />What can I say? It wasn’t what I expected. I loved it. I was completely sucked in and didn’t want to put it down. One might say I was captivated. <br /><br />Now, I have to be careful here not to give anything away – I won’t be getting too specific.<br /><br />Shalini’s writing is such that I truly felt like I knew the characters. Wonderful writing filled the pages and really made an unreal story seem real, like it could be happening right next door and it wouldn’t surprise me at all. It was like Madison and Alexandre were my friends and they were brought to life by the descriptions given to them and how they spoke, the language they used, which was appropriate for their lives/time.<br /><br />There was a sense of adventure about this book. I love the two different timelines and how they complement each other. Each chapter is a switch between Madison and Alexandre and present time and past time. At the end of each chapter something is left hanging and it made me feel quite torn. While reading a chapter I would be thinking about the other character’s story and how I couldn’t wait to get back to it but then I was still immensely enjoying the current story as well. Ah, what a dilemma!! Well no, not really a dilemma because the answer is easy – keep reading as much as you can and as fast as you can so you can finish the book and find out how it all ends.<br /><br />This is the first in the Marchwood series and I will definitely be keeping my eyes out for upcoming books. <br /><br />All in all, not much more to say apart from I loved it!!<br /><br />Many thanks to Shalini for providing me with a copy of <i>Hidden</i> – thanks, Shalini!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16388965388139329544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178500822" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178500822" />
    <a title="Emma Sutherland" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5670066-emma-sutherland"><img alt="Emma Sutherland" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178500822?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Sutherland" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Sutherland" href="/user/show/5670066-emma-sutherland">Emma Sutherland</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5670066-emma-sutherland?shelf=brilliant">brilliant</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178500822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2611063278015546235">Think about the sheer number of times a book has claimed to be the one you won’t be able to put down against how many times that statement has been correct. Many fall at this hurdle of truth but Shalini Boland’s first novel ‘Hidden’ has every right to possess this lofty claim. The twin tales of present day teenager Madison and the 18th century Alexandre weave their way through many twists and turns in their respective time zones and interlock beautifully (the joining of their stories is the book</span>
  <span id="freeText2611063278015546235" style="display:none">Think about the sheer number of times a book has claimed to be the one you won’t be able to put down against how many times that statement has been correct. Many fall at this hurdle of truth but Shalini Boland’s first novel ‘Hidden’ has every right to possess this lofty claim. The twin tales of present day teenager Madison and the 18th century Alexandre weave their way through many twists and turns in their respective time zones and interlock beautifully (the joining of their stories is the books best kept secret so I won’t spoil it for you here). Flowing seamlessly between the present and 1881 keeps both sides of the story unfolding at a steady pace and chapters always end on a cliff-hanger. Descriptive without over explanation, Boland’s characters are vivid on each level. Clear thought about what each person should possess and great visualisation makes each one fold back the pages and builds themselves in the room with you. Madison is beautiful, feisty and full of attitude with an underlying presence of anger and vulnerability; if she were real she’s the girl you’d want as your best friend. Alexandre is outwardly confident, cocky and too handsome for his own good. His privileged rich kid persona is initially a little difficult to feel an affinity with but after soiling his reputation he becomes much more likable as he is shown as being not so perfect after all.<br />‘Hidden’ is aimed at the young adult section but there’s no need to walk on by if, like me, you stopped being a young adult some time ago. Wonderfully written and possessing an absorbing storyline, ‘Hidden’ is this years’ best read. The ending is suitably fitting and Boland has created a sinister undercurrent that bubbles away for what is sure to be a fantastic book two. ‘Hidden’ is the book that will make you want the feistiness of the heroine, the excitement of adventure and the love of the main man. Romantic and thrilling all in one.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2611063278015546235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7904844395826045898" style="display:none">Read the full review on <a href="http://www.paromantasy.com/2011_09_01_archive.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Paromantasy.com</a><br />This book is riddled with mystery, filled with charming romance, with an extra helping of fun and danger thrown into the mix. It's creepy, it's funny, it's romantic, it's fun, it is a thrill ride - so hang on tight and get ready to be taken for tons of twists, turns and bumps when you read Hidden!<br /><br />Two stories come together as past meet present, and reality mixes with legend as numerous mysteries unfold with each page turned.<br /><br />Alexandre who lives in 19th century Paris goes on a archaeological expedition with his family to find a lost city that has been talked about among the ages. Legend has it that this city is cursed. Forgoing the locals warnings, Alexandre moves forward and uncovers the hidden lost city and what he discovers there will forever change his life. <br /><br />Mandy lives in modern day London. Having been in the foster care system with her younger brother, she wonders if life will ever get better. It does when one day a man tells her that she has inherited a fortune, along with a new mansion. Her life is forever changed and she finally feel like she has a normal life, until she makes a haunting discovery in her new home when she discovers vampires in her basement.<br /><br />When all in the world is not what it seems, who can you trust? Each of their lives hangs in the balance in their quest to protect those they love from the men threatening to take it all away.<br />This book has thrills, chills, and heart-warming love! My one complaint is that is takes a while to get to the vampires, but the journey back and forth through time is definitely worth the wait. This YA paranormal romance that will keep you on your toes and racing through the pages. <br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer269504261" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1267794377672095080">This book is very hard for my to rate, mainly because these places won't let my give half stars. I would give this 3.5, I think. As it is, I'll go with three for "liked it" because I can't quite say that I "really liked it."<br/><br/>The pacing of this book felt very weird to me. It didn't feel consistently paced, and it wasn't until after the first hundred pages that I really got into it.<br/><br/>There were elements of the story that I liked. The dual story lines working towards a merging point was good. Madison </span>
  <span id="freeText1267794377672095080" style="display:none">This book is very hard for my to rate, mainly because these places won't let my give half stars. I would give this 3.5, I think. As it is, I'll go with three for "liked it" because I can't quite say that I "really liked it."<br /><br />The pacing of this book felt very weird to me. It didn't feel consistently paced, and it wasn't until after the first hundred pages that I really got into it.<br /><br />There were elements of the story that I liked. The dual story lines working towards a merging point was good. Madison was scrappy and I really liked Alexandre, as he was in the latter portion of the story. I think part of why I couldn't fully connect with the characters is a fault of mine. I didn't understand teenagers when I was one and I struggle with it now, so teen protagonists are hard for me.<br /><br />I would have liked more show and less tell on the actual "falling in love" part of their relationship, but once I got over that, I did feel it. I liked a lot of their exchanges and the Alexandre versus the modern world was very well done.<br /><br />But, I just keep coming back to the pacing. It felt slow, slow and then burst of action and then slow, skimming events, jumping around, then suddenly lots of stuff and tension and drama and... end. I think it would have suited my tastes, and my ever so humble opinion, if the plot and story telling had been more streamlined.<br /><br />That being said, it was a competently told story and fairly written. It's not a bad story or book at all. There were just elements that weren't quite to my reading tastes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1267794377672095080" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

In 1881 Alexandre and his family are investigatin</span>
  <span id="freeText14701509159704164135" style="display:none">I was lucky enough to win an e-copy of this book from a giveaway on Jera’s Jamboree.<br /><br />This book is set in 1881 and the modern-day, I was very intrigued as to how the two would intertwine and this made me want to read on to find out.<br /><br />At this point I enjoyed the modern-day parts the most – Maddy and Ben were fresh and real, they had been through a lot in their short lives so I felt really pleased for them when a surprise revelation changes everything. In 1881 Alexandre and his family are investigating an old legend which takes them to a heart-poundingly scary place deep underground.<br /><br />I found that this book took a while to fully capture my interest, it felt like I spent a long time waiting for the vampires to make an appearance. I was about half way through the book before this happened, but when it did it was so worth the wait because this is when it became eerie and chilling. This is also when I began to see how the two different times would link together.<br /><br />Something I really enjoyed about this story is how the end of each chapter had its own little cliffhanger, this made it very difficult to stop reading and by the end I couldn’t get enough so I was eager to make a start on the second book.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16230268649853306861">This book pops back and forth between the story of Maddy and her brother Ben , who are orphans set in current time, and the story of Alexandre in the 1880's. This is absolutely essential to the story and does not detract at all as some do when they have two alternate story lines going at once. Maddy and her brother live with foster parents and are in constant fear of being separated. When a law firm approaches them and tells them of a proposition put forth by a never known, relative from long ag</span>
  <span id="freeText16230268649853306861" style="display:none">This book pops back and forth between the story of Maddy and her brother Ben , who are orphans set in current time, and the story of Alexandre in the 1880's. This is absolutely essential to the story and does not detract at all as some do when they have two alternate story lines going at once. Maddy and her brother live with foster parents and are in constant fear of being separated. When a law firm approaches them and tells them of a proposition put forth by a never known, relative from long ago, it seems too good to be true. It is also too good to pass up and sends them into a world they never dreamed of. Alexandre is from a wealthy social family, his father an archeologist. A mistake made by Alex causes his whole family to embark on his fathers scheduled expedition and what happens there changes the lives of many for many generations. When the two stories come together all hell will break loose and more than one life may be lost. I loved this book, I'm not a big fan of alternating story lines, but it just works here. The characters are fantastic, the story is fantastic and oh my goodness, the ending left me dying for the next book! Can't wait to see where this goes. Romance, suspense, fun, you name it, this book has it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16230268649853306861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167871840" />
    <a title="Samantha Towle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4072932-samantha-towle"><img alt="Samantha Towle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489752388p2/4072932.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167871840?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samantha Towle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samantha Towle" href="/user/show/4072932-samantha-towle">Samantha Towle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167871840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5362937340182940639">Hidden was everything I hoped it would be, a brand new take on the age old world of vampires. Shalini Boland managed to bring the modern world in to meet with late nineteenth century and make it work perfectly. Vivid descriptions and fluid writing set the scenes, crafting believable and likeable characters. Ben, Madison’s younger brother being one of my favourites, I loved his outlook on the world and life in general! And I also have to say I’m now a little in love with Alexandre!<br/> <br/>It’s is one of</span>
  <span id="freeText5362937340182940639" style="display:none">Hidden was everything I hoped it would be, a brand new take on the age old world of vampires. Shalini Boland managed to bring the modern world in to meet with late nineteenth century and make it work perfectly. Vivid descriptions and fluid writing set the scenes, crafting believable and likeable characters. Ben, Madison’s younger brother being one of my favourites, I loved his outlook on the world and life in general! And I also have to say I’m now a little in love with Alexandre!<br /> <br />It’s is one of the best YA books I have read in a long time and I am eagerly awaiting the next instalment. So all I can say is please hurry Shalini and release the next one!<br /></span>

<div id="review_1678453437" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678453437" />
    <a title="Bridgett Brown" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45846083-bridgett-brown"><img alt="Bridgett Brown" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523068240p2/45846083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678453437?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridgett Brown" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridgett Brown" href="/user/show/45846083-bridgett-brown">Bridgett Brown</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678453437" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10752779178422485057">Shalini Boland does an incredible job with originality and her writing style is spectacular. I love the 2 different timelines and how they complement each other. Each chapter is a switch between Madison and Alexandre and present time and past time. At the end of each chapter something is left hanging. While reading a chapter I would be thinking about the other character's story and how I couldn't wait to get back to it but then I was still immensely enjoying the current story as well.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QZS/fC8kkr6fLWk4Lc71xaOEU43TN7mpdEGma9SrwhBuy6UhVUO2TMRaOSzkCJ4zQ8q7Z/qcjd25wxSUbDFfrA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zTaX1R+GkoKwG16zhlY7RaJX50UHlGeXGGOxKfAtMoLiaY2IZeG2cOtsDqdPkFCzQhkPry4/U+PV4QPWSLevPg==')})
  }
